R)\n\nBased on Part 36-Noise Standards-Aircraft Type Certification, Volume\nIII of the Federal Aviation Regulations.\n\nV\n\n1.0\n\nINTRODUCTION\n\nThis report presents work performed by the General Electric Company\nfor the NASA Lewis Research Center on the Experimental Quiet Engine\nProgram (Contract NAS3-12430).\nIncluded herein are predicted performance data for three experimental\nengine designs two of which were tested in the latter part of the program.\nThese experimental engines provided design data which will potentially allow\nachievement of program objectives. The engines differ primarily in the lownoise design features which have been factored into the fan component designs.\nThe engines incorporating these fans were designed under Phase I of the\nprogram.\nThe flight performance of these engines is based on the predicted\ncomponent performance. These data have been updated to reflect SLS test\nresults obtained from Engines A and C at the General Electric Company Peebles\ntest facility.\n\n2.0\n\nSUMMARY\n\nThree turbofan configurations, each incorporating alternative\nnoise reduction. features, were tested under the Quiet Engine Program.\nPerformance data for these engines are shown over a range of flight\nconditions. The data are presented in tabular form for standard day\nflight inlet conditions. Procedures for estimating nonstandard day\nperformance are shown. Tabular data and calculation procedures to allow\ndetermination of ram recovery, customer bleed, and customer shaft power\nextraction effects on engine performance can be found in the original\n\nPerformance Brochure titled, "Experimental Quiet Engine Program, Predicted\nEngine Performance", dated April 8, 1970. Predicted engine noise levels\nfor representative take-off and approach conditions are provided.\n\n2\n\n3.0\n\nENGINE PERFORMANCE\n\nUnder the Experimental Quiet Engine Program, experimental turbofan\nengines were designed and fabricated to incorporate technology and design\ninnovations to reduce the production and radiation of noise relative to\ncurrent-day or near-future propulsion systems. As part of this program,\nthree different turbofan configurations, each incorporating alternative\nnoise reduction features were tested.\nPredicted performance (based on Sea Level Static test results) for\neach of the three test engine configurations is presented. The three engines\nare each sized for the same uninstalled net thrust at the design point,\nMach 0.82, 35000 feet. The engine characteristics at the design point condition\nare shown below.\n\nEngine\n\nCorrected\nAirflow\n(Lbs/Sec)\n\nFan Pressure\nRatio\n\nNet Thrust\n(Pounds)\n\nSFC\n(Lbs/Hr/Lb)\n\nFan A\n\n961\n\n1.49\n\n4900\n\n0.645\n\nFan B\n\n957\n\n1.48\n\n4900\n\n0.652\n\nFan C\n\n923\n\n1.66\n\n4900\n\n0.673\n\nThe performance at sea level static is established by operation to an\nuninstalled thrust level of 22000 pounds.\nThe fan and fan turbine components on the engines were designed or\n\nmodified for use specifically in the Experimental Quiet Engine Program.\n\nThe\n\nengine performance shown is based on the predicted performance maps for these\ncomponents determined under Phase I of the program and modified to agree with\nthe SLS test results of Quiet Engines A and C. All three engines utilize\nthe CF6/TF39 core gas generator.\n\nSTANDARD DAY PERFORMANCE\nPerformance data are presented for a range of flight conditions over the\nflight envelope shown in Figure 1. S. Standard Atmosphere, 1962, standard day inlet conditions and\n100% ram recovery are assumed. The thrust levels shown are uninstalled\nvalues based on ideal exhaust nozzle performance. Representative test\nengine fan duct and tailpipe pressure losses are included. No customer\nbleed or power extraction is assumed. The fuel lower heating value is\n18400 Btu/lb.\nNONSTANDARD DAY PERFORMANCE\nThe engine control mode has been defined to provide essentially\nconstant maximum thrust over a range of nonstandard day conditions from a\n0\n-20 0 F cold day to a +30.8 F hot day at 10000 feet altitude and sea level\n0\nand a +20.2 F hot day at 20000 feet and above. The deviation of maximum\nthrust from the standard day value is minimal as shown in Table I.\nThe procedure for estimating the specific fuel consumption (SFC) at\nnonstandard-day conditions is shown in the Calculation Procedure.\nINSTALLATION EFFECTS\nData to define installation effects on engine performance at several\nprincipal flight conditions can be found in the original Performance Brochure\ntitled, "Experimental Quiet Engine Program, Predicted Engine Performance ,\ndated April 8, 1970. The data show effects of ram recovery, compressor interstage bleed, and shaft power extraction at maximum power setting.\n\n5\n\nTable I.\n\nAlt\n(Ft)\n\nMO\n\nCold Da\n(Std -20 F)\n\nQuiet Engine Each tabulated performance\npoint is identified by a case number. For first order approximations,\nFor\nlinear interpolation between tabulated conditions may be utilized.\nplotting should be used.\nmore accurate studies, cross\nThe sample calculations which follow show how performance may be\ndetermined at nontabulated values of:\nCorrected Speed\nMach Number\nAltitude\nAmbient Temperature\n\nIntermediate Corrected Speed\nTo determine performance at a corrected speed (PCN*) not tabulated,\nall desired performance parameters can be plotted versus PCN*.\n\nExample:\n\nFor Fan A\nAt MO = 0.70, 35,000 feet Standard Day, Uninstalled\nObtain performance at PCN* = 88.5\n\nFan A\n\nFrom Tabular Data\n\nFrom Cross-plots\n--\n\nCase\n\n166\n\n167\n\n168\n\nPCN*\nFN\n\n89.8\n4960\n\n87.8\n4000\n\n85.6\n3000\n\n88.5\n4280\n\nSFC\n\n.602\n\n.607\n\n.629\n\n.605\n\n9\n\nIntermediate Altitude of Mach Number\nTo determine performance at an altitude or Mach number not tabulated,\nabove and below\nplot the tabulated values at altitudes and/or Mach numbers\nthe desired parameter.\nthe desired flight condition, and cross plot to obtain\nFor example, if performance is desired at 0.8 Mach number at 40,000 feet,\n0.82, and 0.9 at 40,000 ft.\nplot net thrust versus SFC for Mach numbers 0.7,\nThen plot Mach number versus SFC for any desired thrust level (less than\nmaximum) and read SFC for 0.8 Mach number.\n\nFN = Constant\nMO = 0.9\n0.82\n\n0.7\n0.7\n\nSFC\n\nSFC\n\ni\n\nI\n0.82\n\n0.7\n\nFN\n\nI\n0.9\n\nMO\nA similar procedure can be used to determine performance at inter-\n\nmediate altitudes.\nNonstandard Ambient Temperature\nTo determine SFC for a nonstandard day at constant net thrust, use the\nfollowing method.
